< review>
I found this place watching a YouTube video about fried chicken.  I've had popcorn chicken, which is a Taiwanese style fried chicken chicken bits, at several different restaurants. So I want to come here and try it. I actually got several dishes, an order of mild fried Chicken, an order of cold tofu and pork belly over rice.  First of all the mild is very spicy so I would actually wouldn't get it that hot next time. I like the cold tofu which has century eggs and some pork floss with it. I feel like the pork belly over rice was lacking more flavor.<//review>

< Text>
This place is so good! Cute space, kind of cafe like, not too big. You order with the cashier then they bring you your food like at a cafe.

I ordered the Beef Ban Mien and my friend ordered the Popcorn Chicken with Rice. Both were cooked to perfection, super flavorful and not too oily like these items can be. The quality of my noodles was so good - they looked and tasted really authentic.  My friend was sort of dying by how spicy the chicken could get, so I'd suggest not going too spicy.

I would definitely come here again! It was not too crowded (went on a Thursday night) and the food came out quickly. No complaints here!</Text>

<review>Lao Tao is one of my favorite restaurants in all of Los Angeles. I came on a Thursday night (street parking is free starting 8pm, and usually pretty empty). Otherwise there is also a small parking garage right under the restaurant and Lao Tao will validate for up to 45 minutes.

Food-wise, I've had just about everything on the menu. My favorite is by far the popcorn chicken with rice, which comes in many different spice flavors with a nicely cooked egg on top. For the side, I usually get the taiwanese poutine (secret menu item) which is fries covered with pork belly. Customer service was excellent - David is a very polite and friendly person. Space is nice and cozy too, it really feels like home!<//review><Rating>5< /Rating><username>Daniel Kart</username><user_id>106160685931538184219<//user_id>< response>

<Name>MrMoruss78 Mo<//Name>< text>
Great cozy Tawainese that serves quality comfort food. Prices are higher than normal but we're in LA and it was for a friends b-day.

Loa Tao is situated on the second floor of the Far East palza I think it's called.  There is a line that goes out the building, that is for Howling Ray's. Pass up that line, head up the stairs, look to the left and you'll find yourself at Lao Tao eatery.

It was a (southern California) cold, rainy, cloudy day, meaning it was 69 deg with some light sprinkles. So I decided to get hot noodle some with beef broth.  It took a while to get it, but man was it worth it.  The broth had tons of flavor. You can tell the broth had been cooking for a long time. The noodles were great and the big chunks of beef reminded me of the soups my mother used to make.  My wife ended up getting a spicy popcorn chicken bowl with layers of rice, topped off with fried egg, pickled cucumbers, corn, green onions and scrumptious popcorn chicken pieces sprinkled with some hot powder concoction. Yowza!

There are about 5-6 tables here so if you have a big party, messing more than 4 people, good luck. You'll have to wait for other people to leave and go on a table as it is first come first serve.

If I'm in the area I would definitely return here.</text>

<user>100900010911970750562< /user><resp>None</resp>< text>
This is a cool restaurant only about a year old specializing in Taiwanese street food.

It is located in a small mall in the middle of scenic Chinatown which is close to Union train station and the iconic City Hall building.

I went with the sausage party with rice(includes egg).  This tasted delicious with a large amount of thick rice, corn pickles and spicy sauce that was hearty and flavorful.

The popcorn chicken were also fun to eat with nice consistency, texture and crunchiness.

Lao is on the small side seating wise but they do alot of takeout.

They are on the 2nd floor of the same mall with the popular Howlin' Rays on the ground floor.

Definitely worth a visit and something different from the usual chinese places.< /text>

< Text>
Got take out twice here now and I think it's safe to say that I'm a fan. It's a salad place so it's...well...salad. You're not going to get some awesome creative fusion gourmet created food. Just fresh healthy salads that satisfies the tummy. So far I have ordered the Spinach Salad and Caprese Salad and both were delicious. I'm surprised at the quality every time. With that said what I keep coming back to is the vegetarian chili! The chili has a great kick to it and honestly I don't even notice that it's meatless.

I always have a tough time deciding where to eat for lunch and I seem to always feel that I have to settle for something "healthy" so I come to Greenspot. But every time I'm glad I did!< /Text>
